  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d65ed5d8-d3fc-4abd-be58-63af35e853b0'

<span id="freeTextContainer6440349763006761422">Abramm has dedicated the last eight years of his life to becoming worthy to touch and tend the Sacred Flames of Eidon, and he expects to be blessed for his devotion and sacrifice. But on the eve of taking the vows that will irrevocably separate him from the life he was born to--as Abramm Kalladorne, fifth son of the king of Kiriath--he is betrayed by his spiritual mentor a</span>
  <span id="freeText6440349763006761422" style="display:none">Abramm has dedicated the last eight years of his life to becoming worthy to touch and tend the Sacred Flames of Eidon, and he expects to be blessed for his devotion and sacrifice. But on the eve of taking the vows that will irrevocably separate him from the life he was born to--as Abramm Kalladorne, fifth son of the king of Kiriath--he is betrayed by his spiritual mentor and sold into slavery by his brothers.<br /><br />Swept along by the winds of a new destiny, Abramm is forced to compete as a gladiator. When the oppressed masses rally around his success, he discovers his suffering has molded him into something greater than he ever though possible--to serve a purpose he never imagined.<br /><br />Set in a world of swords and cloaks, of glittering palaces and mystical temples, of galley ships and ancient mist-bound cities, <i>The Light of Eidon</i> is the first volume of an epic series, LEGENDS OF THE GUARDIAN-KING.</span>

<div id="review_103136270" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103136270" />
    <a title="Beanbag Love" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2598237-beanbag-love"><img alt="Beanbag Love" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249531311p2/2598237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103136270?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beanbag Love" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beanbag Love" href="/user/show/2598237-beanbag-love">Beanbag Love</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103136270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5217725307502357951">I guess this is a 3.5 for me. I found myself very annoyed at a couple of the main characters and, while I knew their TSTL impulsiveness/stubbornness was necessary for the arc of the story it went on through 90% of the book. A bit much.<br/><br/>Particularly Carissa, the hero's sister. I kept hoping she would meet her doom and she just never did. But then her utter ineptitude and arrogance pretty much created every obstacle poor Abramm and Trap had to overcome so I see the point of her existence, but she r</span>
  <span id="freeText5217725307502357951" style="display:none">I guess this is a 3.5 for me. I found myself very annoyed at a couple of the main characters and, while I knew their TSTL impulsiveness/stubbornness was necessary for the arc of the story it went on through 90% of the book. A bit much.<br /><br />Particularly Carissa, the hero's sister. I kept hoping she would meet her doom and she just never did. But then her utter ineptitude and arrogance pretty much created every obstacle poor Abramm and Trap had to overcome so I see the point of her existence, but she really had zero likability for me. Even after a heroic act of her own she went back to being a monkey wrench. Yes, a monkey wrench divinely implemented, but still...<br /><br />Abramm himself was pretty darn tiresome at times. And that's why I can't muster four stars. He just took too long to get to the point. <br /><br />I did like other characters though. Trap, Cooper and Philip were not only competent, they were extremely likable. <br /><br />It's not a bad book. It was a Kindle freebie and those who like sword and sorcerer fantasy with some religiousity thrown in (think LotR, Narnia) should like it pretty well. I'm not compelled to continue the series though, so take that as you will.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5217725307502357951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6080131521313127049">This is one of the best books I've read in a long time. The story is compelling, the characters engaging, the plot continually twisting and turning, both physically and emotionally. I had a hard time putting this one down. The tale seems to flow almost effortlessly, each plot point encouraging the reader to discover the next. And I say 'almost' because there are some minor bumps in the road: grammatical errors, word repetition… Thankfully, these are few. There is one character, Katahn, who doesn</span>
  <span id="freeText6080131521313127049" style="display:none">This is one of the best books I've read in a long time. The story is compelling, the characters engaging, the plot continually twisting and turning, both physically and emotionally. I had a hard time putting this one down. The tale seems to flow almost effortlessly, each plot point encouraging the reader to discover the next. And I say 'almost' because there are some minor bumps in the road: grammatical errors, word repetition… Thankfully, these are few. There is one character, Katahn, who doesn't seem to stay true to his established pattern of behavior, and it is not clear to me why he made the surprising choices he did later in the story. The hero, however, is so very believable and so very appealing as he makes his way from purpose to despair to hope. The settings are colorful and spectacularly developed, as are the political, religious, and cultural aspects. I thoroughly enjoyed the weaving of fantasy and religion, and what a delight to read a story that tells about wicked, depraved characters without using vile language and gratuitous sex and gore! I look forward to reading more from this author!</span>

<div id="review_143317819" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143317819" />
    <a title="Timothy Ward" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4867952-timothy-ward"><img alt="Timothy Ward" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319336249p2/4867952.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143317819?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Timothy Ward" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Timothy Ward" href="/user/show/4867952-timothy-ward">Timothy Ward</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143317819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13196344391475949301">Karen Hancock has made a significant contribution to the genre of Christian Fantasy with her novel, Light of Eidon. Her allegories are illuminating, accurate to biblical truth and very creative. I enjoyed her characters and how they came from so many viewpoints; they were all true to themselves and left a lasting impression. Her crisp prose never settled for boring description and in doing so kept this world alive. I was glad that she kept me guessing, and even more at how many times I guessed w</span>
  <span id="freeText13196344391475949301" style="display:none">Karen Hancock has made a significant contribution to the genre of Christian Fantasy with her novel, Light of Eidon. Her allegories are illuminating, accurate to biblical truth and very creative. I enjoyed her characters and how they came from so many viewpoints; they were all true to themselves and left a lasting impression. Her crisp prose never settled for boring description and in doing so kept this world alive. I was glad that she kept me guessing, and even more at how many times I guessed wrong. Karen also does a great job keeping you emotionally involved. Her main character, Abramm is a strong protagonist that is well worth being the focal point of a series. On top of all this, I loved her action scenes. This world has a gladiator type system of fighting that makes for great battles, not to mention her unique magic system and monster creations.<br /><br />For anyone writing Christian Fiction, this book provides a great lesson in how to write quality fiction that embraces spiritual truths we all battle. Her characters have depth to their reasoning and in doing so Karen addresses the many concerns people have with embracing a God of grace. I did not find this book preachy — in part because she does not dismiss challenges to biblical faith. Some people accept that gift and others don’t, plain and simple. She is not writing this book to make converts, but rather to show how real the struggle can be and that people can go either way and still be real. You don’t know coming in who will and who won’t, so there is plenty of drama to keep you till the end.<br /><br />The world Karen created is a fantastic example of carrying truths from our world to a fantasy, while using those allegories to express truths in ways you’ll never forget. The golden shield of the Tertsan is an idea I wish I came up with, but I won’t tell you why. The Gospel and how to be saved are both creative and truthful. The opposing religions are complex and not at all straw men or two dimensional in any way. You can really feel what it would be like to live within their religious system and in providing these examples we get a better understanding of the faiths around us. I’m excited to see what adventures are in store for Abramm as he battles against the many enemies left to face in future books.<br /><br />I would have paid for this, but because it was not only free but a very good book, I’ll definitely be buying more of her work in the future. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13196344391475949301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2545287588" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2545287588" />
    <a title="Anna Mussmann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17812040-anna-mussmann"><img alt="Anna Mussmann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585698541p2/17812040.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2545287588?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Mussmann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Mussmann" href="/user/show/17812040-anna-mussmann">Anna Mussmann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2545287588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5944431860726360821">Karen Hancock attempts to blend epic fantasy with Christian allegory. As a fantasy, the book hits all the expected plot notes. I even rather liked the protagonist. However, as an allegory, it ends up teaching really bad theology. I suspect the problems stem from the story concept itself. <br/><br/>The stereotypical plot of an epic fantasy isn’t necessarily a good parallel to the Christian life. The typical epic hero must suffer for a period of time, then defeat the bad guy, and then receive the adoration </span>
  <span id="freeText5944431860726360821" style="display:none">Karen Hancock attempts to blend epic fantasy with Christian allegory. As a fantasy, the book hits all the expected plot notes. I even rather liked the protagonist. However, as an allegory, it ends up teaching really bad theology. I suspect the problems stem from the story concept itself. <br /><br />The stereotypical plot of an epic fantasy isn’t necessarily a good parallel to the Christian life. The typical epic hero must suffer for a period of time, then defeat the bad guy, and then receive the adoration of the masses. He proves that he is “the chosen one” by winning. He usually wins by getting really angry and looking inside himself, upon which he suddenly discovers inner resources that ordinary people would have had to spend their entire lives acquiring. It’s not necessarily a bad plot outline, but it caters to the modern desire to see oneself as the independent hero of one’s own story. Not to mention the modern tendency to feel, deep down, that one deserves to be awesome. <br /><br />Spiritualizing that stereotypical plot results in a story in which converting to the allegorical equivalent of Christianity is perilously close to being a plot device whereby our hero acquires the power to beat up his enemies. It doesn’t help that in this book, suffering causes our characters to profess disbelief in God--and that the author handles that problem by demonstrating that God was using all this suffering to achieve the characters’ eventual temporal triumph. This suggests that we are to identify God’s will by looking for earthly success. It even suggests we have the right to sit in judgment on God, deciding whether the end result of our suffering “proves” it to be worthwhile. Although the characters refer to Scripture, it is their feelings (and their success) that is ultimately the arbiter of truth. <br /><br />Tolkien and Lewis both write tales in which good triumphs over evil, but the flavor is different. Both older authors avoid the hyper-individualism of a lot of modern epic fantasy. Their heroes are part of histories, groups, and cultures; and often it is the weakest members of those groups through whom God works. In contrast, <i>The Light of Eidon</i> falls into the trap of treating all the characters as satellites to our hero. The monolithic mobs riot on cue. The evil soldiers* are apparently all without humanity or hope of redemption. The female characters are completely onenote and kept off-stage for anything important (they quite literally die or pass out). All of this may fit genre expectations--I’m sure that’s why the author follows these patterns--but it’s not helpful to a story intended to express Christianity. It’s true that Christian faith is a relationship between God and an individual. Yet it is lived out in community (the communion of saints), and it is antithetical to the desire for egotistical personal glory.<br /><br />Had the author written this as myth rather than epic fantasy, it might have been easier to see the story as relating purely to "spiritual warfare" rather than earthly life. That might have worked better. <br /><br />*Sidenote: Not to beat up on this book or author, but it’s off-putting to note that the hero is white and the evil people are essentially Middle Eastern. The author would have been wiser to avoid such a trope. Lutheran readers will also note a strong theme of evangelical decision-based theology as well as an authorial distrust of liturgical religion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5944431860726360821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_328603528" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/328603528" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/328603528?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.M. Weiland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.M. Weiland" href="/user/show/2971567-k-m-weiland">K.M. Weiland</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer328603528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3891750362152456152">I honestly didn't go into this book with high expectations. I basically quit reading "faith-based" fiction years ago because I always ended up being disappointed. This one surprised me though. After a slow and occasionally rambling start, it presents a magnificent fantasy world, decent characters, and one of the best conversion scenes I've ever read. Hancock dips and darts around in her lengthy timeline, smoothly sailing over bobbles that would have tripped up most authors. I have to commend her</span>
  <span id="freeText3891750362152456152" style="display:none">I honestly didn't go into this book with high expectations. I basically quit reading "faith-based" fiction years ago because I always ended up being disappointed. This one surprised me though. After a slow and occasionally rambling start, it presents a magnificent fantasy world, decent characters, and one of the best conversion scenes I've ever read. Hancock dips and darts around in her lengthy timeline, smoothly sailing over bobbles that would have tripped up most authors. I have to commend her for her faith-based fantasy world as well. Instead of the usual allegory-ridden tale we get from most Christian-based speculative fiction, she's created a realistic, plausible, in-depth, and entirely relatable and thought-provoking religious society. I'll be reading the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3891750362152456152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2188174847" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2188174847" />
    <a title="Bethany Fehr" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57960109-bethany-fehr"><img alt="Bethany Fehr" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492658318p2/57960109.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2188174847?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bethany Fehr" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bethany Fehr" href="/user/show/57960109-bethany-fehr">Bethany Fehr</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2188174847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12370360703036875230">Finally, a YA Christian novel - and a fantasy novel at that - that is worth reading. It's by no means a perfect book; there are a lot of things it could have done better, but there are also a lot of things this book does right where few of the books in it's genre succeed . <br/><br/>Things this book got right:<br/><br/>In my experience, most fiction labeled "Christian" does not incorporate the faith element well; often the Christian parts of these books have almost no relevance to the story. However, in this book, </span>
  <span id="freeText12370360703036875230" style="display:none">Finally, a YA Christian novel - and a fantasy novel at that - that is worth reading. It's by no means a perfect book; there are a lot of things it could have done better, but there are also a lot of things this book does right where few of the books in it's genre succeed . <br /><br />Things this book got right:<br /><br />In my experience, most fiction labeled "Christian" does not incorporate the faith element well; often the Christian parts of these books have almost no relevance to the story. However, in this book, the main character's spiritual journey is not just a nice subplot, it's necessary to the plot. The story literally would not work without the faith element. <br /><br />This book has one of the best fictional conversion scenes I've read. I was pleasantly surprised at how God-centered the whole message of the book was, especially in that scene. I've found that often the gospel message in Christian fiction is all about what God can do for the characters, and salvation comes across looking cheap as a result. This novel makes it clear that the characters fit into God's plan - not vice versa. On that note, I think the author does an awesome job pulling off that theme without creating a deus ex machina ending. The characters can't make it without God, yet their obedience still plays an essential part in the outcome of the conflict. I also really appreciate that the character's journey toward conversion is realistically led up to. It's not a straight upward climb; there's a lot of backtracking, and the journey takes the length of the book - the story spans around two years - rather than just a chapter or two where everything randomly clicks for the character.<br /><br />The allegory is particularly well done. I appreciated that it wasn't just an obvious retelling of the redemption story. In the timeline of the novel, the story of the cross has already happened, and the allegory focuses on how we can come to know God in our time. The allegory is not super obvious, especially at the beginning. I was expecting the story to be about the main character's spiritual journey, but the author keeps the reader in suspense as to how the character is going to get to the end of that journey. By about the 75% mark, it's pretty clear what's going on, but up to that point, I found I didn't know much that the main character didn't know. The author did quite a good job letting the reader experience the main character's doubts and disillusion along with him, without the answer being obvious. I didn't find myself just waiting around for the character to just hurry up, see the light, and make the obvious decision, because I wasn't sure what form the answer would take myself.<br /><br />After reading a book that deals so well with the character's initial conversion, I'm expecting big things from the next book in the series. From what I've seen of the summary, the next book looks like it'll continue to focus on the spiritual journey started in the first book. I'm looking forward to the rest of the story.<br /><br />I'm also quite impressed with the setting. It's definitely not your stock castles and dragons fantasy land. Actually, this is one of the most realistic fantasy settings I've ever read. The different cultures of the story world are grounded in actual history and human nature. The author chose not to completely reinvent the flora and fauna of her world, and instead incorporated the fantasy element into the details that were relevant to the story. The fantasy element is centered entirely on the spiritual element, which makes the story world more realistic and easier to process than if everything about the world were foreign.<br /><br />Things I thought could have been done better:<br /><br />There were a couple of scenes that deal with the main character having some lustful thoughts that made me uncomfortable. I think that was the intended effect, and while the scenes weren't graphic, for a Christian book, they could have gotten away with less detail. Those scenes are pretty much restricted to two chapters in the middle that aren't essential to the plot.<br /><br />There was one secondary character who was pretty whiny. I pitied her, but her generally caustic attitude made her hard to root for. There are several chapters from her perspective, so it was sometimes a bit painful to be around her for too long.<br /><br />I found the dialogue to be a little on the weak side; it wasn't too bad, but the characters do tend to sound pretty similar. I felt the dialogue wasn't as realistic as it could have been.<br /><br />I often found the setting descriptions a bit hard to follow. There was one action scene where the landscape was important to the characters' plan. I had a really hard time visualizing the surroundings based on the description offered, so I didn't really get what was going on. All the other action scenes made sense, though.<br /><br />There were a bunch of compound adjectives that should have been hyphenated and were instead written as one word (e.g. bluestriped), and I found a few sentences that ended with this punctuation!? I'd like a word with the editor on that one. :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12370360703036875230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15591318710049679110">I downloaded this book for free for my Sony e-reader.<br/><br/>This is a wonderful book that maintained my interest all the way through. It has everything you could want: action, romance, political intrigue. I was a bit shocked and a little upset to find that this book is considered to have heavy Christian overtones.   <span id="freeText15591318710049679110" style="display:none">I downloaded this book for free for my Sony e-reader.<br /><br />This is a wonderful book that maintained my interest all the way through. It has everything you could want: action, romance, political intrigue. I was a bit shocked and a little upset to find that this book is considered to have heavy Christian overtones. This is a fantasy book, and many fantasy characters believe in a god or gods, so I guess that's why it was more palatable to me than a strictly Christian book. The religious aspects of it didn't bother me for that very reason.<br /><br />Abramm is about to take his priestly vows, forsaking his claim to the throne forever, but fate, or his god Eidon, has other plans. Gripped with madness his brother and the current king forces him into exile, which leads Abramm into slavery. He is not strong enough to interest the Gamers, but someone buys him for his talents as a scribe. Unfortunately, he has attracted the interest of one Gamer, and ends up as a gladiator anyway. While this story is about the struggle Abramm must endure to survive, it is also about his struggle with his faith as he travels from devout believer to cynical skeptic.<br /><br />As a fantasy book, this is one of the best I've read in a longtime, so I went ahead and bought the second in the series.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18324691782539116600">As a big fan of Christian fantasy, this book was pleasantly surprising. It's definitely not the YA high-action, low-dialogue fantasy that I was expecting. It's actually a lot deeper and meant for an older audience. <br/><p>The main character, Eldrin (renamed Abramm later on), is the fifth son of the king of Kiriath. As a child, he didn't excel in fencing, like his younger brother Gillard, because his love was in religion and history. He joined the religious group known as the Matatio at a young age, giv</p></span>
  <span id="freeText18324691782539116600" style="display:none">As a big fan of Christian fantasy, this book was pleasantly surprising. It's definitely not the YA high-action, low-dialogue fantasy that I was expecting. It's actually a lot deeper and meant for an older audience. <br /><p>The main character, Eldrin (renamed Abramm later on), is the fifth son of the king of Kiriath. As a child, he didn't excel in fencing, like his younger brother Gillard, because his love was in religion and history. He joined the religious group known as the Matatio at a young age, giving up his rights as a prince. <br /></p><p> At the beginning of the book, Eldrin is twenty-one and just about to take his final vows to become a full Brother and leave his past life behind him forever. When he gets to Kiriath, he discovers that the throne isn't so far away from him as it used to be, and his life turns upside-down. <br /></p><p>I'd recommend this to anyone 16+ who's looking for a good, epic Christian fantasy fix. This book stands pretty well on its own, and anyone who wants more can read the next three in the series as well.</p></span>

<div id="review_255051996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/255051996" />
    <a title="Sunny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6881533-sunny"><img alt="Sunny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320855707p2/6881533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/255051996?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sunny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sunny" href="/user/show/6881533-sunny">Sunny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12938270-light-of-eidon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer255051996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5874314488056128019">I had to get past my frustration with the main character. I understand Karen Hancock may have wanted to show his struggle to the way of the Light. However, it was irritating to read the thoughts of the character as he came off as a prideful idiot. Even when it was obvious, he kept sticking his head in the sand. Now this would have been fine if it had only lasted about 10 - 20% of the book. No, this lasted for about 75 - 80% of the book. And the main character's sister was just as bad. Neither we</span>
  <span id="freeText5874314488056128019" style="display:none">I had to get past my frustration with the main character. I understand Karen Hancock may have wanted to show his struggle to the way of the Light. However, it was irritating to read the thoughts of the character as he came off as a prideful idiot. Even when it was obvious, he kept sticking his head in the sand. Now this would have been fine if it had only lasted about 10 - 20% of the book. No, this lasted for about 75 - 80% of the book. And the main character's sister was just as bad. Neither were very likable characters. What kept me going were the supporting characters as they had more life than those two. This book showed the turmoil one can encounter when everything they had once believed in has been torn asunder. It demonstrated how one has to pick of the pieces after everything has been blown apart. The book was not entertaining enough for me to want to read any more from the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5874314488056128019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1986339005" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1986339005" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5532305-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517174155p2/5532305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1986339005?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/5532305-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1986339005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2490727244804091189">If this book was a movie, it'd be better than Gladiator. There. I said it. Why? Because this book has purpose. The main character, Abramm (Eldrin) goes through some major life struggles. Struggles many of us could relate to. Things don't go our way, we get frustrated - we wished it had gone the way we envisioned it, but it doesn't. We keep thinking we're making the right decisions but we aren't. Who hasn't gone through that at some point? The struggles Abramm deals with are real, but they're exp</span>
  <span id="freeText2490727244804091189" style="display:none">If this book was a movie, it'd be better than Gladiator. There. I said it. Why? Because this book has purpose. The main character, Abramm (Eldrin) goes through some major life struggles. Struggles many of us could relate to. Things don't go our way, we get frustrated - we wished it had gone the way we envisioned it, but it doesn't. We keep thinking we're making the right decisions but we aren't. Who hasn't gone through that at some point? The struggles Abramm deals with are real, but they're expertly woven into a story involving kings, slaves, gladiators, foreign lands, and hope. Most of all, <b>hope</b>.<br /><br />This is the second book I've read by Karen Hancock and I'm constantly amazed at the way she vividly describes things in such a way as to make it <i>pleasing</i> to read. The text flows so well that if you're not looking for it, you might miss it. One such example, <blockquote>"The courtiers postured and bowed and fluttered, the men directed here and there by the women, tripping and reeling exaggeratedly as they slopped wine down the fronts of their doublets."</blockquote> And there is action, lots of action. Swordplay, daggers, giant evil birds, epic battles, and more. As with the first book I read by Hancock, <i>Arena</i>, the beginning is quite slow, building up the characters to be memorable, but picks up later on. She definitely knows how to create a climax to a book, and as this one builds, it's really hard to put down. While this is the first book in the Light of Eidon series, there is a definite resolution to the story. Again - so many books or movies nowadays just cut off in the middle of things promising the resolution in part two or three, so it's a pleasant surprise when there is finalization to the plot you've been reading for 400 pages.<br /><br />Finally, while this is a Christian book series, you're not beat over the head with Christianity. If you're a Christian, you'll understand all of the parallels, but if you're not, you'll more than likely just enjoy a great book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2490727244804091189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_312608092" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312608092" />
    <a title="Benjamin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4809742-benjamin"><img alt="Benjamin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456090093p2/4809742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/312608092?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin" href="/user/show/4809742-benjamin">Benjamin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312608092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3894933218514320318">I had a hard time caring about the main character. It's clear that his Ben Hur story arc and his macho transformation are supposed to be the stuff of epic page turners, but the guy is just really, really bland. The book climaxes with the epiphany that his greatest obstacle is pride and self-reliance and that everything he's accomplished is actually his deity acting through him; the character's own actions only ever get in the way. I doubt it was the intention, but this plot point turns the clich</span>
  <span id="freeText3894933218514320318" style="display:none">I had a hard time caring about the main character. It's clear that his Ben Hur story arc and his macho transformation are supposed to be the stuff of epic page turners, but the guy is just really, really bland. The book climaxes with the epiphany that his greatest obstacle is pride and self-reliance and that everything he's accomplished is actually his deity acting through him; the character's own actions only ever get in the way. I doubt it was the intention, but this plot point turns the cliche fated-to-be-great trope of typical fantasy on its head by making the character's very blandness into the inborn talent that allows him to fulfill destiny. This interpretation significantly improved my enjoyment of an otherwise forgettable novel.<br /><br />Apropos of nothing, there are a fair number of specific elements in the book that I am familiar with only from the Wheel of Time series. These include the word shadowspawn, using the phrase "wool-headed" to indicate stupidity, dragon brands on arms, a strong-willed female character who expresses anger by spitting, and a couple others that passed by before I started keeping a list.<br /><br />my favorite quote: "Instinct whirled him faster than thought."</span>
  <a data-text-id="3894933218514320318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11709036816183428108">I was about a third of the way into this one before I decided it was a pseudo-Christian allegory; I realize now that that was the whole point, but if you start out thinking you're just in for some basic run-of-the-mill fantasy, it'll be a kind of surprise. Change a few proper nouns and some minor details, and you've got yourself a world beset by evil where Christian faith is all but outlawed but is really the only right answer. The main difference between being a Terstan and being a Christian is</span>
  <span id="freeText11709036816183428108" style="display:none">I was about a third of the way into this one before I decided it was a pseudo-Christian allegory; I realize now that that was the whole point, but if you start out thinking you're just in for some basic run-of-the-mill fantasy, it'll be a kind of surprise. Change a few proper nouns and some minor details, and you've got yourself a world beset by evil where Christian faith is all but outlawed but is really the only right answer. The main difference between being a Terstan and being a Christian is that Terstans get magic powers; I'm sure churches in our own world would be much more popular if that little bonus was included in membership.<br />The story itself borrowed quite a bit from other stories, not least of all the movie Gladiator. If you forgive that fact, it's enjoyable enough, but still somewhat contrived and heavy-handed with its religious message. Great if you like that, just OK if you don't mind it. </span>

New terminology, relating to the complexities of the faith systems introduced to us and of the different cultures mentioned. As the story unfolded, the characters were easy to grab onto, relate to, feel with. <br /><br />I enjoyed this book, and now that I know there are 3 more that continue the story, I am excited to read them too - to follow the life of Abramm Kalladorne as he struggles to become the man he's destined to be. </span>

  <span id="freeText5358609608139010137" style="display:none">A decent, if predictable, adventure story. There was definitely a strong 'been there, read that' factor throughout the book which led to the predictability. My biggest complaint though is that the religious overtones and parallels to Christianity are as subtle as a nuclear explosion. <div id="review_2723852716" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2723852716" />
    <a title="Kes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70325177-kes"><img alt="Kes" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2723852716?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kes" href="/user/show/70325177-kes">Kes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8228646-light-of-eidon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70325177-kes?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70325177-kes?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2723852716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12115193388208406087">This started off feeling rather Christian-inspired: we start with Eldrin, a novice of Eidon. Eidon is the god a monotheistic state religion, and he's associated with light, flames, being the defender of man, etc. Eidon stands in opposition to the Terstan religion, which marks its followers with a golden shieldmark. The religion of Eidon teaches that the Terstan adherents are associated with darkness etc.<br/><br/>Eldrin - known at birth as Abram - was the fifth in line to the throne; we start with him fin</span>
  <span id="freeText12115193388208406087" style="display:none">This started off feeling rather Christian-inspired: we start with Eldrin, a novice of Eidon. Eidon is the god a monotheistic state religion, and he's associated with light, flames, being the defender of man, etc. Eidon stands in opposition to the Terstan religion, which marks its followers with a golden shieldmark. The religion of Eidon teaches that the Terstan adherents are associated with darkness etc.<br /><br />Eldrin - known at birth as Abram - was the fifth in line to the throne; we start with him finding out that his father and older brothers have died. He is now second in line (with another brother behind him). This obviously creates consternation, as he renounced his titles before entering the priesthood. We then discover that there's a sinister plot afoot, resulting in Eldrin being shipped off to foreign lands as a slave. Eldrin then <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[becomes a gladiator in those foreign lands, improves his swordplay dramatically, and we end the book with him contributing to overthrowing the kingdom there and converting everyone to Terstan <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />There's an interesting mix of religion and magic that's not really explored in the first book. Faith appears to give special powers to their adherents (e.g. manifesting a shield, summoning demon birds). There are magics like illusions, or portals that link places together.<br /><br />The worldbuilding feels ok - it felt like a fantasy version of Christianity (there are ports, deserts and desert tribes, etc), and that wasn't my cup of tea. The plot line (someone weak becoming strong / discovering faith) was standard. It's not a bad book, just a boring one. Unfortunately, I'm not tempted to move on to the sequels.<br /><br />2/5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="12115193388208406087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3632075019" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3632075019" />
    <a title="K L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77289651-k-l"><img alt="K L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521522587p2/77289651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3632075019?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K L" href="/user/show/77289651-k-l">K L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3632075019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4759588151691470418">While I recommend this novel, I couldn't finish it quickly. I had a nagging frustration but couldn't quite place why or what it was. First off, it's difficult to tell where the story is going. Karen Hancock builds the plot slowly, and it spans years. I realized that's what problem was: <i>The Light of Eidon</i> feels like two books smashed into one. The complexity, which is the book's greatest strength, is also its Achilles Heel. <br/><br/>The world-building, for example, is phenomenal. The countries, customs, a</span>
  <span id="freeText4759588151691470418" style="display:none">While I recommend this novel, I couldn't finish it quickly. I had a nagging frustration but couldn't quite place why or what it was. First off, it's difficult to tell where the story is going. Karen Hancock builds the plot slowly, and it spans years. I realized that's what problem was: <i>The Light of Eidon</i> feels like two books smashed into one. The complexity, which is the book's greatest strength, is also its Achilles Heel. <br /><br />The world-building, for example, is phenomenal. The countries, customs, and languages all read like real places one could walk right into. However, the intricate details can also bog down the plot. OK, the harbor and billowing sails are beautiful, but the main character is in danger! <br /><br />The plot flows surprisingly smoothly for all the events and years Karen Hancock fit in-between 400 pages. Most authors couldn't have pulled it off. That being said, I read this book in small bite-sized chunks rather than racing through to the end; it was simply too much. As I said, the slow-burn plot is its both best and worst quality.<br /><br />Only several chapters into the second book in the series, I found it much better. The pacing issues in #1 are not as evident in #2. I've heard the books get better as they go on, and while I'm only halfway through the second installment, this seems to be true.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4759588151691470418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1835078284824791084">Wow! Epic Christian Fantasy novel that didn't hold back...yes, please! I actually gave this book 4.5 stars. This world is complex and very well developed. The different people groups, customs and beliefs, histories and cultures are all intricate and fully developed. The plot was action packed and had me guessing more than once. The timing was great and I had know idea we would end up where we did. There were many scenes that I absolutely loved! The beauty of friendship built through trauma was f</span>
  <span id="freeText1835078284824791084" style="display:none">Wow! Epic Christian Fantasy novel that didn't hold back...yes, please! I actually gave this book 4.5 stars. This world is complex and very well developed. The different people groups, customs and beliefs, histories and cultures are all intricate and fully developed. The plot was action packed and had me guessing more than once. The timing was great and I had know idea we would end up where we did. There were many scenes that I absolutely loved! The beauty of friendship built through trauma was fantastic. I enjoyed most all the characters except for Carissa. She drove me insane... Evil was depicted as evil and not glossed over at all. I was surprised by the reality and gruesomeness of evil that this story brought to life. It made this novel feel so real. The characters journey was intense and their transformations were exciting and inspiring to be a part of. From a Christian perspective, the truth of the gospel really shines nicely and I appreciate the enforcement that salvation is never earned, but freely given to all who would receive it. I am very excited to continue forward to the second novel in this series. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rkkgJcqiQrZhnb8A49ooLCPxybFU1FEsfPioju6XHEStO1kX1fjfAKoByhIMT7tzz+j7dmkh/7qrimlNrzUH/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KLkA9RDkO814xZawr6DHmtxYZZ+FQULjxVyt/yy8cJQry3nHD76me7NZ46JANVTFMEFXWLi07HUSLmw8bR5rLA==')})
  }
